\n1625: #### New child process `'spawn'` event\n1626: \n1627: Instances of `ChildProcess` now emit a new `'spawn'` event once the child process has spawned successfully.\n1628: \n1629: If emitted, the `'spawn'` event comes before all other events and before any data is received via `stdout` or `stderr`.\n1630: \n1631: The `'spawn'` event will fire regardless of whether an error occurs **within** the spawned process.\n1632: For example, if `bash some-command` spawns successfully, the `'spawn'` event will fire, though `bash` may fail to spawn `some-command`.\n1633: This caveat also applies when
